The Condition of Equality: Definitions Must Be Coextensive and Converse
Explains the condition that the definition must equal the defined in generality and specificity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a definition must be exactly equal in generality and specificity to the defined, and how the properties of muṭṭarid and munʿakis ensure this.

Core Idea
A good definition is a perfect mirror — neither too wide nor too narrow.

In logic, a definition must capture exactly the defined term — no more, no less. This lesson explains the crucial condition of equality (musāwāh). If a definition is too broad, it includes non-defined items; if too narrow, it excludes some of the defined. The terms muṭṭarid (coextensive) and munʿakis (converse) describe these two sides of the same requirement.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the author's argument.
Notice the use of parentheses — they indicate the author's own interjections.
2
Identify the central condition
The passage states that the definition must equal the defined in generality and specificity. Identify why this is necessary.
3
Understand the consequences of inequality
The text gives two cases: if the definition is more general, it fails to prevent non-defined items from entering; if more specific, it fails to include all defined individuals.
4
Learn the terms muṭṭarid and munʿakis
Muṭṭarid means the definition applies wherever the defined applies. Munʿakis means the definition applies to everything the defined applies to. Together they ensure perfect equality.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question about muṭṭarid to confirm you've understood the property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بد ( إشارة إلى شرط آخر للمعرف، أي لا بد من أن يساويه في العموم والخصوص ليحصل) به (التميز إذ (لولاه أي لولا كونه مساوياً (لدخل فيه غير المعرف) على تقدير كونه أعم مطلقاً أو من وجه ) فلم يكن مانعاً من دخول غير المعرف فيه (و) لا (مطرداً) وهو أن يكون بحيث كل ما صدق على شيء صدق عليه المعرف أيضاً ) أو خرج عنه بعض أفراده ) على تقدير كونه أخص إما مطلقاً أو من وجه فلم يكن جامعاً لجميع أفراد المعرف (و) لا (منعكساً) وهو أن يكون بحيث يصدق على كل ما صدق عليه المعرف
And it is necessary (indicating another condition for the definition, i.e., it must equal it in generality and specificity so that) by it (distinction is achieved, because if not, i.e., if it were not equal, then what is other than the defined would enter into it) on the assumption that it is more general absolutely or in some respect, so it would not be a preventer of the entry of what is other than the defined into it (and) it would not be (coextensive (muṭṭarid)) meaning that it is such that whatever it applies to, the definition also applies to it (or some of its individuals would be excluded) on the assumption that it is more specific either absolutely or in some respect, so it would not be comprehensive of all individuals of the defined (and) it would not be (converse (munʿakis)) meaning that it is such that it applies to everything to which the definition applies
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage presents the second condition for a definition: it must be equal (musāwī) in generality and specificity to the defined. The author explains that if the definition is more general (aʿamm), it would include things that are not part of the defined, thus failing to prevent the entry of non-defined items (not manʿiy). If it is more specific (akhass), it would exclude some individuals of the defined, thus not being comprehensive (not jāmiʿ). Two crucial properties are then introduced: muṭṭarid (coextensive) means that wherever the definition applies, the defined also applies (ensuring comprehensiveness); and munʿakis (converse) means that wherever the defined applies, the definition also applies (ensuring exclusivity).

Key Terms
مساواة
مطرد
منعكس
جامع
مانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A definition can be more general or more specific than the defined and still be valid.
Correction: This passage shows that a definition must be exactly equal in generality and specificity; otherwise it fails to distinguish or cover all instances.

Checkpoint
What does the term muṭṭarid mean in the context of definition?
A) The definition applies to everything the defined applies to
B) The definition is more specific than the defined
C) The definition excludes non-defined items
D) The definition is comprehensive of all individuals

Key Takeaway
A correct definition must be coextensive (muṭṭarid) and converse (munʿakis), meaning it applies to exactly the same set as the defined term.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe your own Islamic faith (iman), is your definition exactly equal to what Allah and His Messenger defined? Or do you inadvertently add conditions from your culture or subtract conditions due to convenience? Where might your definition be more specific or more general than revelation? Commit to correcting that today.
?
Think of a person you disagree with on a religious issue. Could the disagreement stem from differing definitions that are not coextensive? How can you apply the conditions of muṭṭarid and munʿakis to ensure you are discussing the same defined term? What step will you take this week to clarify definitions before debating?
?
Do you define yourself as a 'righteous person' (saliḥ)? Is that label muṭṭarid and munʿakis with the Shari'ah definition? Consider an area where your actions claim the label but your heart or behavior does not match. Ask Allah to make your definition of yourself equal to what He defines you to be.

The Necessity of a Coextensive Differentiator
Establishes the necessity of a coextensive differentiator and its role in distinguishing hadd from rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why every valid definition requires a coextensive differentiator and how the nature of that differentiator determines whether the definition is a limit (hadd) or a description (rasm).

Core Idea
A definition must have a differentiator that exactly matches the definiendum.

Before we can classify definitions into complete or incomplete, we must understand the foundational requirement: every definition needs a differentiator that is coextensive with the definiendum. This differentiator can be either essential or accidental, and that distinction gives rise to the two primary types of definition: hadd and rasm. In this lesson, we examine this necessary condition and the basic classification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the key terms: معرف, مميز, مساو, حد, رسم.
2
Identify the necessary condition
Look for the phrase 'لا بد فيه من مميز مساو' and understand that the differentiator must be coextensive.
3
Distinguish hadd from rasm
Notice that the differentiator being essential yields hadd, while accidental yields rasm.
4
Understand the commentator's clarification
The commentator explains that the differentiator can differ in essence (for composite definitions) or in consideration (for simple terms).
This clarifies how a single term can serve as a differentiator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد السادس - المقصد الثاني : المعرف تجب معرفته رسماً، ولا بد فيه أي في المعرف من مميز مساو للمعرف فإن كان المميز ذاتياً سمي المعرف حداً وإلا رسماً وعلى التقديرين فإن ذكر فيه تمام الذاتي المشترك بينه وبين غيره المسمى بالجنس القريب فتام إما حد تام مركب من الجنس والفصل القريبين وإما رسم تام مركب من الخاصة والجنس القريب وإلا فناقص إما حد ناقص سواء كان بالفصل وحده أو مع الجنس البعيد، أو العرض العام عند من يجوز أخذه في الحد، وإما رسم ناقص سواء كان بالخاصة وحدها، أو مع الجنس البعيد أو العرض العام عند من يجوز أخذه في الرسم. قوله : ( ولا بد فيه من مميز مسار إلخ) إما مغايراً له بالذات كما في التعريف بالمركب، أو بالاعتبار كما في التعريف بالمفرد، فهو من حيث إنه معرف ظرف له من حيث كونه مميزاً مساوياً، وقد يقال : الكلام على حذف المضاف أي في حصول المعرف أو شأنه .
The sixth observation - the second aim: The definiendum must be known by description. It is necessary in it, i.e. in the definition, a differentiator coextensive with the definiendum. If the differentiator is essential, the definition is called a limit (hadd), otherwise a description (rasm). In both cases, if the common essential shared with others called the proximate genus is mentioned in full, then it is complete: either a complete limit composed of the proximate genus and proximate differentia, or a complete description composed of the specific property and the proximate genus. Otherwise it is incomplete: either an incomplete limit, whether by the differentia alone or with the remote genus, or by the universal accident according to those who permit its inclusion in the limit; or an incomplete description, whether by the specific property alone, or with the remote genus or the universal accident according to those who permit its inclusion in the description. His statement: 'There must be a differentiator ... etc.' either being different in essence as in definition by a composite, or by consideration as in definition by a simple term. So it is, insofar as it is a definition, a vessel for it, insofar as it is a coextensive differentiator. And it is said: the speech is on the ellipsis of the complement, i.e., in the occurrence of the definition or its matter.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions for a valid definition (ta'rif) and classifies definitions into two main categories: essential definition (hadd) and accidental definition (rasm). It begins by stating that the definiendum must be known by description (rasm), but then establishes the necessity of a differentiator (mumayyiz) that is coextensive (musawin) with the definiendum. This differentiator can be either essential (dhati) or accidental (aradi). If essential, the definition is a limit (hadd); if accidental, it is a description (rasm). The passage then subdivides each into complete (tamm) and incomplete (naqis). A complete definition mentions the full genus (jins qarib) and differentia (fasl) or specific property (khassa). An incomplete definition omits one of these elements. The commentator explains that the differentiator can be identical in essence or in consideration, and clarifies that the phrase 'in it' refers to the occurrence of the definition.

Key Terms
معرف
مميز
مساو
حد
رسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any distinguishing feature is sufficient for a definition.
Correction: The differentiator must be coextensive (musāwin), meaning it applies to exactly the same set of things as the definiendum.

Checkpoint
What determines whether a definition is called a limit (hadd) or a description (rasm)?
A) Whether the differentiator is coextensive or not
B) Whether the differentiator is essential or accidental
C) Whether the definition is complete or incomplete
D) Whether the genus is proximate or remote

Key Takeaway
Every definition needs a coextensive differentiator; its essentiality determines whether the definition is a hadd or rasm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a person you have defined by a single accidental attribute—perhaps their mistakes, appearance, or social status. How might your definition be a rasm rather than a hadd? What would it take to redefine them by an essential differentiator?
?
Your definition of yourself often relies on accidental differentiators (your job, relationships, failures). If you could only define yourself by an essential differentiator—something that is truly inseparable from your essence—what would that definition be? Are you willing to live by that definition today?
?
Consider your definition of 'righteousness' (taqwa). Does your differentiator exactly match what the Qur'an says, or have you added accidental conditions? What would need to change for your definition to be coextensive?

Complete and Incomplete Definitions
Subclassifies hadd and rasm into complete and incomplete based on mention of the proximate genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how definitions are further subdivided into complete (tāmm) and incomplete (nāqiṣ) based on the inclusion of the proximate genus and other elements.

Core Idea
A complete definition mentions the proximate genus; an incomplete one omits it.

Having learned the basic distinction between hadd and rasm, we now explore how each can be either complete or incomplete. The completeness depends on whether the definition includes the full common essential (proximate genus) shared with other things. This lesson lays out the four possible types: complete hadd, complete rasm, incomplete hadd, and incomplete rasm, along with the permissible components for incomplete definitions.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification passage
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'وعلى التقديرين' and its translation. Notice the structure: first the condition for completeness, then the two complete types, then the incomplete types.
2
Identify the condition for completeness
A definition is complete if it mentions 'تمام الذاتي المشترك' which is the proximate genus.
3
List the four types
Complete hadd: proximate genus + proximate differentia. Complete rasm: proximate genus + specific property. Incomplete hadd: differentia alone, with remote genus, or with universal accident. Incomplete rasm: specific property alone, with remote genus, or with universal accident.
Note that universal accident is allowed only for those who permit it in definitions.
4
Understand the significance
This classification helps in analyzing definitions for logical rigor: a complete definition is more precise, but incomplete ones are still valid in certain contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد السادس - المقصد الثاني : المعرف تجب معرفته رسماً، ولا بد فيه أي في المعرف من مميز مساو للمعرف فإن كان المميز ذاتياً سمي المعرف حداً وإلا رسماً وعلى التقديرين فإن ذكر فيه تمام الذاتي المشترك بينه وبين غيره المسمى بالجنس القريب فتام إما حد تام مركب من الجنس والفصل القريبين وإما رسم تام مركب من الخاصة والجنس القريب وإلا فناقص إما حد ناقص سواء كان بالفصل وحده أو مع الجنس البعيد، أو العرض العام عند من يجوز أخذه في الحد، وإما رسم ناقص سواء كان بالخاصة وحدها، أو مع الجنس البعيد أو العرض العام عند من يجوز أخذه في الرسم. قوله : ( ولا بد فيه من مميز مسار إلخ) إما مغايراً له بالذات كما في التعريف بالمركب، أو بالاعتبار كما في التعريف بالمفرد، فهو من حيث إنه معرف ظرف له من حيث كونه مميزاً مساوياً، وقد يقال : الكلام على حذف المضاف أي في حصول المعرف أو شأنه .
The sixth observation - the second aim: The definiendum must be known by description. It is necessary in it, i.e. in the definition, a differentiator coextensive with the definiendum. If the differentiator is essential, the definition is called a limit (hadd), otherwise a description (rasm). In both cases, if the common essential shared with others called the proximate genus is mentioned in full, then it is complete: either a complete limit composed of the proximate genus and proximate differentia, or a complete description composed of the specific property and the proximate genus. Otherwise it is incomplete: either an incomplete limit, whether by the differentia alone or with the remote genus, or by the universal accident according to those who permit its inclusion in the limit; or an incomplete description, whether by the specific property alone, or with the remote genus or the universal accident according to those who permit its inclusion in the description. His statement: 'There must be a differentiator ... etc.' either being different in essence as in definition by a composite, or by consideration as in definition by a simple term. So it is, insofar as it is a definition, a vessel for it, insofar as it is a coextensive differentiator. And it is said: the speech is on the ellipsis of the complement, i.e., in the occurrence of the definition or its matter.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions for a valid definition (ta'rif) and classifies definitions into two main categories: essential definition (hadd) and accidental definition (rasm). It begins by stating that the definiendum must be known by description (rasm), but then establishes the necessity of a differentiator (mumayyiz) that is coextensive (musawin) with the definiendum. This differentiator can be either essential (dhati) or accidental (aradi). If essential, the definition is a limit (hadd); if accidental, it is a description (rasm). An incomplete definition omits one of these elements. The commentator explains that the differentiator can be identical in essence or in consideration, and clarifies that the phrase 'in it' refers to the occurrence of the definition.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a complete limit (hadd tamm)?
A) Differentia alone
B) Specific property alone
C) Proximate genus + proximate differentia
D) Proximate genus + specific property

Key Takeaway
A definition is complete if it includes the proximate genus; otherwise it is incomplete, with various permissible components.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you explain the core beliefs of Islam to someone, do you ensure your definition includes the 'proximate genus' — the essential truths you share with all Muslims? Or do you settle for an incomplete description that might distort the meaning? What is one incomplete definition you have been using that needs to be made complete?
?
The lesson shows that omitting the proximate genus makes a definition incomplete. In your journey of learning about Allah's names and attributes, have you ever omitted an essential aspect, leading to an incomplete understanding? How can you seek a more complete definition by including that missing element?
?
An incomplete definition is still considered valid in logic. But in your spiritual life, are you content with incomplete definitions that lack precision? For example, when defining 'faith' (īmān), do you include all its pillars or just a few? What step will you take this week to move from an incomplete to a complete definition?

The Paradox of Prior Conception in Definition
Examines the paradox of prior conception and the differentiator's role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the epistemological problem that a definition must presuppose some prior conception of the definiendum to be informative, and how scholars address whether the differentiator must be part of the definition.

Core Idea
You must already know something to be taught anything new.

This passage tackles a foundational puzzle in logic: if a definition is supposed to tell us what something is, how can we recognize it as a definition unless we already have some idea of the thing? The commentator walks through this paradox using the example of a triangle and also examines whether the differentiator in a definition must be a separate part or can be the whole phrase.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the English translation. Notice the two main topics: the paradox of prior conception, and the discussion of the differentiator as part or whole.
The passage is dense; do not worry about understanding every detail on first read.
2
Identify the paradox
The passage says definition is like a request. To request something, you must already have some conception of it. So how can a definition provide that conception? Focus on the triangle example to see the problem.
The example: someone knows a triangle is a polygon but does not know what distinguishes it from a circle.
3
Analyze the differentiator as part
The text then debates whether the differentiator must be a part of the definition. It gives the bat example (flying viviparous) where the whole phrase distinguishes, not a single part.
This shows that the differentiator can be the entire definition, not necessarily a component.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you grasp the core paradox. Then reflect on how this problem arises in everyday definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإن كان المميز إلخ ) وإذا اجتمع المميزان يسمى رسماً اكمل من الحد، وهو خارج عن القسمين لأن القسم المميز الواحد وإدخاله في القسم الثاني بأن يراد في القسم الأول إن كان المميز ذاتيا فقط غير صحيح، لأنه حصر القسم الثاني في الرسم التام المركب من الجنس القريب، والخاصة والرسم الناقض المنقسم إلى ما يكون بالخاصة وحدها، أو بالخاصة والجنس البعيد أو العرض العام، والرسم الأكمل ليس شيئاً منهما . موقوفة على تصوره بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه، والتوفيق بين كلاميه مشكل لأن التعريف من قبيل الطلب فيلزم أن يمتاز المطلوب التصوري قبل التعريف عن جميع ما عداه ومن لم يعرف ما هذه بعد أن المثلث من الأشكال المضلعة كيف يقال : إنه تصور المثلث بوجه يمتاز عن جميع . عداه ولا شك أن التعريف على الوجه الذي صور إنما يتأتى بالنسبة إلى من علم أن الدائرة ليست بمضلعة، وعلم أن شكلاً من الأشكال يقال له المثلث ولم يعرف أنه غير الدائرة أو عينها، أو علم مجملا أنه غيرها وطلب أن يتصور بوجه مخصوص يمتاز به عنها، ولا شك أنه في الحالة لم يتصوره بوجه يمتاز عن جميع. ما عداه فليتأمل. قوله ولا بد فيه من مميز وظاهر العبارة يشعر بلزوم جزئية المميز مع جواز التعريف بالمفرد، وعلى تقدير وجوب كونه مركباً، لا يلزم أن يكون المميز المساوي جزءاً له، بل يجوز أن يحصل التمييز التام من المجموع كما في تعريف الخفاش الطائر الولود، فقيل : ما ذكره بناء على الأعم الأغلب وقيل المراد في شأن المعرف. قوله : ( فإن كان ذاتياً سمي (حداً) أي إن كان المميز ذاتياً فقط، فالمركب من جميع الذاتيات والعرضيات مندرج في قوله، وإلا سمي رسماً على ما صرحوا من أنه رسم تام، لكنه أكمل من الحد التام. قوله : ( أو العرض العام عند من يجوز أخذه في الحد المركب من الفصل القريب، والعرض العام رسم ناقص على ما يستفاد من كلام المطالع وحد ناقص على ما ذكره الشارح ها هنا، وهو الموافق لما صرح به الرازي في شرح المطالع، حيث أبطل كلام مصنفه بأن الفصل وحده إذا أفاد
His statement: 'if the differentiator ... etc.' If two differentiators come together, it is called a description more complete than the limit, and it is outside the two divisions because the division is for a single differentiator. Inserting it into the second division by intending in the first division that if the differentiator is only essential is not correct, because the second division is restricted to the complete description composed of the proximate genus and the specific property, and the incomplete description divided into what is by the specific property alone, or by the specific property and the remote genus, or the universal accident; the more complete description is not one of them. It is dependent on its conception in a way that distinguishes it from everything else. Reconciling the two statements is problematic because definition is of the type of request, so it necessitates that the conceptual object sought is distinguished before definition from everything else. Whoever does not know what this is, after [learning that] the triangle is among polygonal shapes, how can it be said: he conceived the triangle in a way distinguishing it from everything else? And there is no doubt that the definition in the manner he pictured only occurs for someone who knows that the circle is not polygonal, and knows that a shape is called a triangle and does not know whether it is other than the circle or identical to it, or knows in general that it is other than it and seeks to conceive it in a specific manner distinguished from it. And there is no doubt that in this case he did not conceive it in a way distinguishing it from everything else, so let him reflect. His statement: 'and it is necessary in it a differentiator' and the apparent wording suggests the necessity of the differentiator being a part, while allowing definition by a simple term. Assuming it must be composite, it does not require that the coextensive differentiator be a part of it; rather complete differentiation can be obtained from the whole, as in the definition of the bat as a flying viviparous (animal). So it is said: what he mentioned is based on the more common, and it is said: the intended meaning concerns the matter of the definition. His statement: 'if it is essential, it is called a limit' i.e., if the differentiator is only essential, then the composite of all essentials and accidentals is included in his statement, otherwise it is called a description according to what they stated that it is a complete description, but it is more complete than the complete limit. His statement: 'or the universal accident according to those who permit its inclusion in the limit' – the composite of the proximate differentia and the universal accident is an incomplete description based on what is understood from the speech of al-Mutala', and an incomplete limit according to what the commentator mentioned here, which is in agreement with what al-Razi stated in his commentary on al-Mutala', where he invalidated the wording of its author by saying that the differentia alone if it benefits...
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage discusses the epistemological problem of definition: for a definition to be informative, the definiendum must already be conceived in a way that distinguishes it from everything else, yet definition aims to provide that distinction. This creates a paradox, illustrated by the triangle example. The commentator then addresses whether the differentiator must be a part of the definition, concluding that it need not be; the whole phrase can serve. Finally, he comments on classifications involving the universal accident (arad 'am), noting different views on whether such composites are limits or descriptions.

Key Terms
مميز
تصور
تمييز
ذاتي
عرضي
خاصة
جنس

عرض عام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The paradox of prior conception shows that definition is impossible.
Correction: The paradox does not invalidate definition; it only shows that definition requires some prior knowledge. The definition then refines that knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the definition of a triangle problematic for someone who only knows it is a polygon?
A) The triangle has no parts
B) The person already knows the triangle fully
C) The person does not yet distinguish the triangle from other polygons
D) The definition uses the genus but not the differentia

Key Takeaway
A definition presupposes some prior conception of the thing defined; complete novelty cannot be communicated through definition alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that simply hearing a lecture or reading a book would give you new, deep understanding—only to find yourself unchanged? Could it be that you lacked the prior distinct conception needed to truly receive that knowledge? What are you doing to prepare your inner framework before seeking knowledge?
?
The paradox shows that definition cannot create a completely new conception from nothing. When it comes to knowing Allah, you are told He is known through His signs and attributes. But if you have no innate sense of the Divine, how can any description truly enlighten you? Do you believe that you already have a faint, innate recognition of God (فطرة)—or do you expect proof to create belief from scratch?
?
The bat is defined as 'flying viviparous.' This whole phrase gives a distinct conception. In your own life, what 'whole phrases' or experiences have given you a distinct understanding of a concept—like justice, patience, or love—that no single word could convey? Are you content with single-term answers, or do you pursue the fuller composite that yields real distinction?

Definitions of Composite and Simple Concepts
Clarifies when a limit (hadd) is possible and when it is not.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why composite concepts can be defined by their parts while simple concepts cannot, and how the definability of a concept depends on its composition.

Core Idea
Composite concepts are definable; simple concepts are not.

This passage from the Sharh al-Mawaqif explains a foundational logical principle: any concept that is composite (made of parts) can be defined by listing those parts, either completely or partially. In contrast, a simple concept has no parts, so it cannot be defined at all. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper theological and philosophical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
2
Identify composite and simple categories
Look for the terms 'مركب' (composite) and 'بسيط' (simple). Notice how the passage treats them differently.
The passage contrasts composites with simples in definition.
3
Examine the condition for composites
Note that composites are definable only if they are not intuitively conceived (بديهي التصور). If intuitive, no definition is needed.
4
Understand why simples are indefinable
The passage explicitly says a simple concept cannot be defined because it has no part (جزء).
This is a key logical point.
5
Consider the special mixture case
The passage also discusses something composed of both composite and simple elements, and whether it can be defined.
This clarifies the boundaries of definability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البعيد أو العرض العام عند من يجوز أخذه في الرسم (والمركب) إذا لم يكن بديهي التصور يحد بأجزائه حداً تاماً وناقصاً (دون البسيط) فإنه لا يمكن تحديده، إذ لا جزء له (فإن تركب عنهما عن المركب والبسيط غيرهما) ولا يكون ذلك الغير التصور (حد بهما وإلا فلا يحد بهما إذ لم يقعا جزءاً لشيء (وكل) متصور (كسبي) مركب أو بسيط له خاصة شاملة لازمة (بينة) بحيث يكون تصورها مستلزما لتصوره (يرسم) (وإلا) أي وإن لم تكن له خاصة كذلك (فلا) يرسم (فإن كان) ذلك الكسبي الذي له تلك الخاصة (مركباً أمكن رسمه التام بتركيب جنسه القريب مع خاصته) وإلا فالناقص. قوله : ( والمركب إلخ) بيان لما يحد وما لا يحد وما يحد به وما لا يحد به . قوله : ( وإلا فلا يحد بهما أي لا يقعان في الحد ، فلا يردان مجموع الحيوان الناطق لم يقع جزء الشيء مع أنه يحد به الإنسان .
The remote or the universal accident according to those who permit its inclusion in the description. And the composite, if it is not intuitively conceivable, is defined by its parts with a complete and incomplete limit – unlike the simple, for it cannot be defined, since it has no part. If it is composed of both the composite and the simple, something else [results], and that other is not conceptual; it is defined by them, otherwise it is not defined by them, since they are not part of anything. And every conceptual acquired (kasbi) thing, composite or simple, having a comprehensive necessary specific property that is evident, such that its conception entails its conception, is described (yursam). Otherwise, if it does not have such a specific property, it is not described. If that acquired thing having that specific property is composite, its complete description is possible by composing its proximate genus with its specific property; otherwise, the incomplete. His statement: 'and the composite ... etc.' is an explanation of what is defined and what is not defined, and what it is defined by and what it is not defined by. His statement: 'otherwise it is not defined by them' i.e., they do not occur in the limit, so the composite 'animal rational' is not excluded, for it did not occur as a part of a thing despite being used to define human.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage sets out the rules for defining composite and simple concepts. A composite concept that is not intuitively known can be defined by its parts, giving either a complete or incomplete limit. A simple concept cannot be defined because it has no parts. If something is composed of both composite and simple, it is defined by them. Additionally, any acquired concept that has a specific property (khassa) that is coextensive and clearly entailing the concept can be described (rasm), otherwise it cannot. The commentary clarifies that the limits are about what can be defined and what can be used as definiens, and resolves a potential objection concerning the definition of human by 'animal rational'.

بسيط

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All concepts can be defined by giving a limit.
Correction: Only composite concepts can be defined; simple concepts cannot, because they lack parts.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why cannot a simple concept be defined by a limit?
A) Because it is intuitively known
B) Because it has no parts
C) Because it lacks a specific property
D) Because it is always acquired

Key Takeaway
A concept can be defined by a limit only if it is composite; a simple concept is indefinable by limit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Descriptions of Acquired Concepts
Sets out the rules for when a description (rasm) is possible and how to construct it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how acquired concepts that have a distinctive property can be described (rasm) by referencing that property, and the conditions for such description.

Core Idea
Acquired concepts with a clear distinguishing property can be described.

After discussing limits (hadd), the text turns to descriptions (rasm). A description is an alternative way to clarify a concept when a full limit is not possible. The passage explains that any concept that is acquired (not innate) and has a specific property that is coextensive and evident can be described by that property. This is particularly useful for simple concepts that cannot be defined by limit.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Focus on the section starting with 'وكل متصور كسبي' up to the end. Read the translation carefully.
2
Identify conditions for description
Look for the three conditions: concept must be acquired (كسبي), have a comprehensive necessary specific property (خاصة), and that property must be evident (بينة) and entailing the concept.
3
Distinguish composite vs simple in description
Note that for composite concepts, a complete description uses proximate genus and specific property; for simple concepts, only incomplete.
4
Examine the exception
If the concept lacks such a property, it cannot be described at all.
5
Read the commentator's clarification
The commentator connects description back to limits and resolves an objection about 'animal rational' defining human.

Definition by Example and Analogy
Introduces definition by example and analogy and its classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what definition by example and analogy are, and when they count as valid incomplete descriptions (rasm naqis).

Core Idea
A definition by example works only if the similarity distinguishes the definiendum.

The author introduces two additional types of definition: by example and by analogy. These are not arbitrary illustrations; they can function as real definitions if the similarity between the definiendum and the example serves to distinguish it. This lesson explains the rule and gives examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own structure come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins by naming two new types, then gives the condition.
2
Identify the two types
The passage first presents definition by example (tamthil) and notes it is really definition by analogy (tashbih). Understand the relationship.
3
Examine the condition
The key condition: if the similarity helps to distinguish the definiendum, it becomes a specific property and yields an incomplete description (rasm naqis). Otherwise it is not valid.
This is the central rule of the passage.
4
Study the examples
The commentary explains how 'noun is like Zayd' and 'knowledge is like light' work. Note the point of similarity in each case.
These examples clarify how the similarity functions as a distinguishing property.
5
Reflect on the classification
Ask yourself: why is this called a rasm naqis? How does it fit into the four divisions of definition mentioned earlier?
The passage explicitly states it falls under those four divisions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهاهنا نوعان آخران من التعريف الأول) التعريف ( بالمثال ( سواء كان جزئياً للمعرف، كقولك : الاسم كزيد والفعل كضرب أو لا يكون جزئياً له، كقولك : العلم كالنور والجهل كالظلمة ( وهو بالحقيقة تعريف بالمشابهة ) ذلك المعرف وبين المثال ( فإن كانت تلك المشابهة ( مفيدة للتميز فهي خاصة) لذلك المعرف ( فيكون) التعريف بها (رسماً ناقصاً) داخلاً في الأقسام الأربعة المذكورة للمعرف ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم تكن المشابهة مفيدة للتميز (لم تصلح. قوله : (تعريف بالمشابهة) أي بما به المشابهة فإن تعريف الاسم بزيد تعريف بكونه مستقلاً بالمفهومية، غير مقترن بأحد الأزمنة، وكذا تعريف العلم بالنور تعريف بكونه موجباً للانكشاف وقس على ذلك . التمييز الحدي، فهو مع شيء آخر أولى بذلك نعم في كلامه بحث ظاهر، وهو أنه لو صح ما ذكره، يوجب أن يكون المركب من جميع الذاتيات والعرضيات حداً، وليس كذلك بل أطبقوا على أنه رسم تام وقيل المركب من الفصل القريب والعرض العام رسم تام. قوله : (إذ لم يقعا جزءاً لشيء) فيه مناقشة لأن مجموع الحيوان الناطق يصدق عليه أنه مركب لم يقع جزءاً لشيء، مع أنه يحد به الإنسان إلا أن يقال : التركيب يعم التركيب من أجزائه . قوله : ( كقولك الاسم (كزيد المشبه هو الماهية الكلية للاسم والمشبه به هو زيد ووجه الشبه هو المعاني المعتبرة في الماهية من الاستقلال وعدم الاقتران بالزمان .
And here are two other types of definition: first, definition by example (tamthil), whether it is a particular of the definiendum, as you say 'the noun is like Zayd' and 'the verb is like daraba', or not a particular of it, as you say 'knowledge is like light' and 'ignorance is like darkness'. It is in reality a definition by similarity between that definiendum and the example. If that similarity is beneficial for distinction, then it is a specific property for that definiendum, so the definition by it becomes an incomplete description (rasm naqis) falling under the four mentioned divisions of the definition. Otherwise, if the similarity is not beneficial for distinction, it is not valid. His statement: 'definition by similarity' i.e., by that in which the similarity lies, for definition of the noun by Zayd is a definition by its being independent in meaning, not associated with any of the tenses. Similarly, definition of knowledge by light is a definition by its causing disclosure, and so on. The distinguishing limit, so it is with something else more entitled to that. Yes, in his speech there is an apparent investigation, which is that if what he mentioned were correct, it would require that the composite of all essentials and accidentals be a limit, but it is not so; rather they unanimously agree that it is a complete description, and it is said the composite of the proximate differentia and the universal accident is a complete description. His statement: 'since they are not part of anything' – there is a discussion, because the composite 'animal rational' is true that it is a composite that is not part of anything, yet it is used to define human, unless it is said that composition includes composition from its parts. His statement: 'as you say the noun is like Zayd' – the compared is the universal essence of the noun, and the compared-to is Zayd, and the point of similarity is the meanings considered in the essence, namely independence and non-association with time.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage introduces two additional types of definition: definition by example (tamthil) and definition by analogy (tashbih). It explains that definition by example is essentially a definition based on similarity. If the similarity effectively distinguishes the definiendum, it qualifies as an incomplete accidental definition (rasm naqis). The commentator illustrates with examples: the definition of a noun by the example 'Zayd' highlights its independence from tense, and the definition of knowledge by 'light' highlights its property of disclosure. The passage then addresses a related objection about the composite of all essential and accidental properties being considered a limit, but the consensus is that it is a complete description. It also comments on the phrase 'since they are not part of anything' regarding the definition of human by 'animal rational', and explains the structure of the example with 'Zayd'.

تعريف بالمشابهة

تمييز
خاصة
ماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Definition by example is only an informal illustration and never a real definition.
Correction: If the similarity provides a distinguishing property, definition by example is a valid incomplete description (rasm naqis).

Checkpoint

A) When the example is a particular of the definiendum
B) When the similarity between definiendum and example is useful for distinction
C) When the example is not a particular of the definiendum
D) When the definition includes both genus and differentia

Key Takeaway
Definition by example counts as an incomplete description only if the similarity it highlights is unique to the definiendum.

Logic and Technical Terms
beginner
5 min
Composite and Simple Concepts in Definition
Defines what can and cannot be defined by hadd, distinguishing composite from simple.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why simple concepts cannot be defined by hadd (essential definition) and how composite concepts are defined by their parts.

Core Idea
Simple concepts have no parts, so they cannot be defined by essential definition.

In this passage, the author establishes a foundational principle: only composite concepts that are not intuitively known can be defined by their parts. Simple concepts, lacking parts altogether, are indefinable by hadd. This lesson unpacks that principle and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the types of concepts
Notice the passage distinguishes composite concepts that are not intuitive from simple concepts. Find the conditions for definition.
The key is that simple concepts have no parts.
3
Understand the condition for defining
The passage adds a condition: if composite and simple together compose something else, that something else is not defined by them. Consider the example of 'rational animal'.
4
Reflect on the discussion
The commentary notes a potential objection about 'rational animal' defining human. Understand how it is resolved.
Composition includes composition from parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد السادس - المقصد الثاني : المعرف تجب معرفته البعيد أو العرض العام عند من يجوز أخذه في الرسم (والمركب) إذا لم يكن بديهي التصور (يحد) بأجزائه حداً تاماً وناقصاً (دون البسيط) فإنه لا يمكن تحديده، إذ لا جزء له (فإن تركب عنهما عن المركب والبسيط (غيرهما) ولا يكون ذلك الغير التصور (حد بهما وإلا فلا يحد بهما إذ لم يقعا جزءاً لشيء قوله : (والمركب إلخ) بيان لما يحد وما لا يحد وما يحد به وما لا يحد به . قوله : (وإلا فلا يحد بهما) أي لا يقعان في الحد ، فلا يردان مجموع الحيوان الناطق لم يقع جزء الشيء مع أنه يحد به الإنسان . قوله : (إذ لم يقعا جزءاً لشيء) فيه مناقشة لأن مجموع الحيوان الناطق يصدق عليه أنه مركب لم يقع جزءاً لشيء، مع أنه يحد به الإنسان إلا أن يقال : التركيب يعم التركيب من أجزائه .
The Sixth Observatory - The Second Purpose: The definition that must be known. The remote [genus] or the common accident, according to one who permits taking it in the definition-by-accident (al-rasm), and the composite (al-murakkab) if it is not intuitive in conception (badīhī al-taṣawwur) is defined (yuḥaddu) by its parts with a complete and incomplete definition (ḥadd tāmm wa nāqiṣ), except the simple (al-basīṭ) for it cannot be defined, since it has no part. Then if [the composite and the simple] compose something other than them, that other is not [properly] a conception to be defined by them, otherwise it is not defined by them because they did not occur as a part of anything. His saying: (and the composite etc.) is an explanation of what is defined and what is not defined, and by what it is defined and by what it is not defined. His saying: (otherwise it is not defined by them) means they do not occur in the definition, so the composite of 'rational animal' (majmūʿ al-ḥayawān al-nāṭiq) is not objected, for it did not occur as a part of something, even though the human is defined by it. His saying: (because they did not occur as a part of anything) contains a discussion, because the composite of 'rational animal' is described as a composite that did not occur as a part of anything, while it is used to define human, unless it is said: composition includes composition from its parts.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of definition (ḥadd) and its conditions. It begins by stating that the distant genus or common accident, for those who allow it in definition-by-accident, and the composite concept, if not intuitively known, can be defined by its parts in a complete or incomplete definition. The simple concept, however, cannot be defined because it has no parts. If a composite and a simple together compose something other than themselves, that other thing is not properly a concept to be defined by them; if they do not compose something else, they cannot define it because they are not parts of it. The commentary explains that the phrase 'otherwise it is not defined by them' means that the two items do not function as parts in a definition, using the example of 'rational animal' which, though composed, does not serve as a part of another thing, yet it defines human. A discussion follows noting that 'rational animal' is a composite that is not a part of anything, yet it defines human, but the response is that composition here refers to composition from parts, so 'rational animal' is defined by its parts (animal and rational) and thus is composite in that sense.

رسم
بسيط
مركب
بديهي
كسبي
خاصة
لازمة
بينة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Simple concepts can be defined by listing their properties or attributes.
Correction: Simple concepts have no parts, so they cannot be defined by essential definition (ḥadd). They can only be known intuitively or described by accidents (rasm).

Checkpoint
Why can a simple concept (al-basīṭ) not be defined?
A) Because it is not intuitive
B) Because it has no parts
C) Because it is too abstract
D) Because definition requires a genus and differentia

Key Takeaway
Only composite concepts can be defined by essential definition because they have parts; simple concepts, lacking parts, cannot be defined.

?
The passage discusses a condition for using composites in definition. When you learn about Islam from scholars, do you passively accept definitions or do you examine whether they are properly built on parts? How can you apply this lesson's intellectual rigor to your own study of aqeedah? What is one specific concept you will analyze this week?

Conditions for a Valid Definition by Accident (al-Rasm)
Sanusi enumerates the conditions for a valid definition by accident and its two types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three conditions that a property must meet to serve in a definition by accident (al-rasm) and the two types of rasm (complete and incomplete).

Core Idea
A definition by accident requires a property that is exclusive, comprehensive, and evidently necessary.

In logic, a definition by accident (al-rasm) identifies something through a non-essential but distinguishing property. But not every property works—it must satisfy strict conditions. This passage from Sanusi lays out those conditions and how they determine whether a definition is complete or incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall meaning. Notice the key terms: خاصة (exclusive), شاملة (comprehensive), لازمة بينة (evidently necessary).
The passage is dense but clear.
2
Identify the three conditions
Find the three conditions for a property (خاصة) to be used in a definition by accident: it must be exclusive (مانعة), comprehensive (شاملة), and its necessity must be evident (لازمة بينة).
These conditions ensure the property uniquely identifies the thing and leads the mind to it.
3
Distinguish complete vs. incomplete rasm
See how the text differentiates: if the acquired conception is composite, it can have a complete definition by accident (rasm tāmm) by combining its proximate genus with the property; otherwise, it receives only an incomplete definition (rasm nāqiṣ).
The completeness depends on whether the thing has parts (composite) or not (simple).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل متصور كسبي مركب أو بسيط له خاصة شاملة لازمة بينة بحيث يكون تصورها مستلزما لتصوره يرسم وإلا فلا يرسم فإن كان ذلك الكسبي الذي له تلك الخاصة مركباً أمكن رسمه التام بتركيب جنسه القريب مع خاصته وإلا فالناقص قوله : (وكل متصور إلخ) بيان لما يرسم وما لا يرسم ولما يرسم به وما لا يرسم به . قوله : (خاصة) ليكون مانعاً شاملة لجميع أفراده ليكون جامعاً لازمة، أي في الذهن بينة اللزوم ليتحقق الانتقال منها إليه .
And every acquired conception (kasmī), composite or simple, that has a proper accident (khāṣṣa) that is comprehensive, necessary (lāzima), and evident (bayyina) such that its conception entails the conception of it, is defined by accident (yursamu), otherwise it is not defined by accident. If that acquired thing that has that proper accident is composite, its complete definition by accident is possible by combining its proximate genus with its proper accident, otherwise the incomplete [one]. His saying: (and every conception etc.) is an explanation of what is defined by accident and what is not, and by what it is defined by accident and by what it is not. His saying: (proper accident) so that it is exclusive, comprehensive of all its individuals so that it is inclusive, necessary, i.e., in the mind evident in necessity so that the transition from it to it is verified.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions and types of definition by accident (al-rasm). It states that any acquired conception (whether composite or simple) can be defined by accident if it has a proper accident (khāṣṣa) that is comprehensive (shāmila) of all individuals, necessary (lāzima) in the mind, and evident (bayyina) in its implication, such that conceiving the proper accident necessarily leads to conceiving the defined thing. If not, it cannot be defined by accident. If the acquired conception is composite, it can receive a complete definition by accident (rasm tāmm) by combining its proximate genus with its proper accident; otherwise, it receives only an incomplete definition. The commentary clarifies that the proper accident must be exclusive (manīʿ) to prevent non-members, comprehensive to include all members, and its necessity must be evident in the mind to allow transition from the accident to the defined thing.

Key Terms
خاصة
شاملة
لازمة
بينة
رسم
كسبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any accidental property can serve in a definition by accident.
Correction: The property must be exclusive, comprehensive, and its implication must be evident in the mind. Otherwise, it does not yield a valid definition by accident.

Checkpoint
What are the three conditions for a property (khāṣṣa) to be used in a definition by accident?
A) Universal, necessary, and eternal
B) Exclusive, comprehensive, and evident in necessity
C) Essential, primary, and intuitive
D) Particular, accidental, and immediate

Key Takeaway
A valid definition by accident depends on a property that is exclusive, comprehensive, and evidently necessary, leading to either a complete or incomplete definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own study of Islamic concepts, do you ensure that the defining properties you use are both exclusive (preventing wrong inclusions) and comprehensive (covering all correct cases)? Think of a specific term you have learned and check whether your definition meets these conditions. How will you refine it?
?
This lesson shows that a valid definition requires the property to be evidently necessary in the mind. Is your understanding of the oneness of Allah (tawheed) based on properties that are evident and necessary to you? What would it take for your conception to be as clear as the 'evident necessity' described here?

Definition by Example (al-Ta'rīf bi-al-Mithāl)
Explains definition by example and its classification as a type of definition by accident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how definition by example works as a form of definition by accident, and the condition that the resemblance must be distinctive.

Core Idea
Definition by example is definition by resemblance, valid only if the resemblance distinguishes the defined.

This lesson introduces definition by example, one of the additional types of definition discussed in Islamic logic. The passage clarifies that giving an example is not a separate kind but reduces to definition by accident when the resemblance serves to distinguish the defined. We will explore why examples like 'the noun is like Zayd' are used and how they relate to the four main divisions of definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the terms 'تعريف بالمثال' and 'تعريف بالمشابهة'.
2
Identify the two types of examples
Notice that examples can be particular to the defined (e.g., 'the noun is like Zayd') or not particular (e.g., 'knowledge is like light'). The passage specifies that both are covered under definition by example.
3
Understand the validity condition
The key is whether the resemblance between the defined and the example is useful for distinction. If yes, it becomes a proper accident (خاصة) and qualifies as an incomplete definition by accident (رسم ناقص). If not, it is unsuitable.
4
Reflect on the scholarly investigation
Consider the objection that if the author's view were correct, any composite of essences and accidents would be a definition. The passage explains that consensus considers such a composite a complete definition by accident, not a definition. Also, note why examples are used: because particulars are easier to perceive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهاهنا نوعان آخران من التعريف الأول) التعريف ( بالمثال ( سواء كان جزئياً للمعرف، كقولك : الاسم كزيد والفعل كضرب أو لا يكون جزئياً له، كقولك : العلم كالنور والجهل كالظلمة ( وهو بالحقيقة تعريف بالمشابهة ) ذلك المعرف وبين المثال ( فإن كانت تلك المشابهة ( مفيدة للتميز فهي خاصة) لذلك المعرف ( فيكون) التعريف بها (رسماً ناقصاً) داخلاً في الأقسام الأربعة المذكورة للمعرف ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم تكن المشابهة مفيدة للتميز (لم تصلح للتعريف بها قوله : (تعريف بالمشابهة) أي بما به المشابهة فإن تعريف الاسم بزيد تعريف بكونه مستقلاً بالمفهومية، غير مقترن بأحد الأزمنة، وكذا تعريف العلم بالنور تعريف بكونه موجباً للانكشاف وقس على ذلك . التمييز الحدي، فهو مع شيء آخر أولى بذلك نعم في كلامه بحث ظاهر، وهو أنه لو صح ما ذكره، يوجب أن يكون المركب من جميع الذاتيات والعرضيات حداً، وليس كذلك بل أطبقوا على أنه رسم تام وقيل المركب من الفصل القريب والعرض العام رسم تام. قوله : ( كقولك الاسم (كزيد المشبه هو الماهية الكلية للاسم والمشبه به هو زيد ووجه الشبه هو المعاني المعتبرة في الماهية من الاستقلال وعدم الاقتران بالزمان . قوله : ( ولما كان استئناس إلخ ) دفع توهم أنه لما كان في الحقيقة تعريفاً بالمشابهة، فلم ارتكبوا التسامح ؟ وهرفوا بالمثال ووجه الاستئناس كون الجزئيات أول المدركات .
And here are two other types of definition: first, definition by example (al-taʿrīf bi-al-mithāl), whether it is particular to the defined (e.g., you say: the noun is like Zayd, and the verb is like ḍaraba) or not particular to it (e.g., you say: knowledge is like light, and ignorance is like darkness). And it is in reality a definition by resemblance (al-mushābaha) between that defined and the example. If that resemblance is useful for distinction, then it is a proper accident (khāṣṣa) for that defined, so the definition by it is an incomplete definition by accident (rasm nāqiṣ) falling within the four mentioned divisions of definition. Otherwise, i.e., if the resemblance is not useful for distinction, it is not suitable for definition by it. His saying: (definition by resemblance) i.e., by that with which resemblance [occurs]. For the definition of the noun by Zayd is a definition by its being independent in conceptuality, not associated with any time; likewise the definition of knowledge by light is a definition by its being a cause of uncovering, and analogously. The distinction [achieved] by the definition is with something else more appropriate. Yes, in his speech there is an apparent investigation: that if what he mentioned were correct, it would necessitate that the composite of all essential and accidental properties be a definition, but it is not so; rather, they unanimously agree that it is a complete definition by accident, and it is said that the composite of the proximate differentia and the common accident is a complete definition by accident. His saying: (like you say: the noun is like Zayd) the resembled is the universal essence of the noun, and the resembling is Zayd, and the aspect of resemblance is the meanings considered in the essence, i.e., independence and non-association with time. His saying: (and when there is familiarity etc.) is a rebuttal of the misconception that since it is in reality a definition by resemblance, why did they commit tolerance and use examples? The reason for familiarity is that particulars are the first things perceived.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage discusses definition by example (al-taʿrīf bi-al-mithāl) as one of two additional types of definition. It explains that the example may be a particular instance of the defined (e.g., defining 'noun' by 'Zayd') or not (e.g., defining 'knowledge' by 'light'). In reality, this is definition by resemblance between the defined and the example. If the resemblance serves to distinguish the defined, it functions as a proper accident (khāṣṣa) and qualifies as an incomplete definition by accident (rasm nāqiṣ), falling within the four previously mentioned divisions. If not, it is unsuitable. The commentary clarifies that 'definition by resemblance' means the resemblance itself; defining 'noun' by 'Zayd' highlights the noun's independence from time, and defining 'knowledge' by 'light' highlights its revelatory nature. The commentary then notes a scholarly investigation: if the author's view were correct, any composite of essences and accidents would be a definition, but the consensus is that such a composite is a complete rasm. Finally, it addresses why examples are used despite being mere resemblance: because particular instances are easier for the mind to grasp.

Key Terms
تعريف بالمثال
تعريف بالمشابهة
خاصة
رسم ناقص
التمييز الحدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Definition by example is a completely independent type of definition.
Correction: It is actually definition by resemblance and becomes definition by accident if the resemblance is distinctive.

Checkpoint
What determines whether a definition by example is a valid definition?
A) The example must be a particular of the defined
B) The resemblance must be useful for distinction
C) The definition must be from essence to essence
D) The example must be a cause of the defined

Key Takeaway
Definition by example is only valid as a definition when the resemblance it provides is sufficient to distinguish the defined from other things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a concept in your deen that you rely on an example to understand—like 'iman is light.' Is that resemblance truly distinctive, or could it mislead you? What would it take for you to verify your understanding from a precise definition? Commit to seeking a deeper explanation before the day ends.
?
When you define Allah's attributes by comparing them to human qualities (istiḍrār), how do you ensure that the resemblance is not taken literally? Are you comfortable with the limits of such examples, or do they lead you to false assumptions? Examine your heart: are there any attributes you have imagined incorrectly?
?
You have just learned that a definition by example is valid only if it distinguishes the defined. In your own life, have you ever held a belief based on an example that later turned out to be false because you assumed a resemblance that didn't really discriminate? What will you do to prevent that from happening again?

What is a Verbal Definition?
Defines verbal definition and argues it is not a real conceptual definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a verbal definition only clarifies the referent of a word and does not produce new conceptual knowledge.

Core Idea
Verbal definition is about words, not concepts.

We often think definitions give us new concepts. But in logic, a verbal definition only resolves ambiguity about which meaning a word refers to. This lesson explains the nature of verbal definition and why it is not a real conceptual definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of verbal definition
Read the Arabic passage where the author defines verbal definition as interpreting an unclear word with a clearer word, like 'al-ghaḍanfar is the lion'.
Notice the example: الغضنفر الأسد.
2
Contrast with real definition
Real definition aims to produce a new conception; verbal definition only determines the referent of a word.
The text says: وليس هذا تعريفاً حقيقياً يراد به إفادة تصور غير حاصل.
3
Examine the objection
Some might argue that the concept as signified by the first word differs from that signified by the second, making it a real definition. Identify this objection in the text.
Look for: ما قيل: من أن المفهوم من حيث إنه مدلول اللفظ الأول مغاير لنفسه من حيث إنه مدلول اللفظ الثاني.
4
Understand the refutation
The author refutes by saying verbal definition only presents the essence of the first word, not a different concept under a description.
The refutation ends with: ففيه أن المفاد من التعريف اللفظي إحضار ذات اللفظ الأول بتوسط اللفظ الثاني.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( والثاني التعريف اللفظي وهو أن لا يكون اللفظ واضح الدلالة ) على معنى ( فيفسر بلفظ أوضح دلالة ) على ذلك المعنى كقولك : الغضنفر الأسد وليس هذا تعريفاً حقيقياً يراد به إفادة تصور غير حاصل، إنما المراد تعيين ما وضع له لفظ الغضنفر من بين سائر المعاني، ليلتفت إلى ذلك قوله : ( وليس هذا تعريفاً حقيقياً إلخ إذ التعريف الحقيقي ما يكون تصوره سبباً لتصور آخر، ولما لم يكن في التعريف اللفظي المغايرة إلا من حيث اللفظ، لا يتحقق ها هنا تصوران متغايران بالذات، أو بالاعتبار فضلاً عن كون أحدهما سبباً للآخر، وما قيل: من أن المفهوم من حيث إنه مدلول اللفظ الأول مغاير لنفسه من حيث إنه مدلول اللفظ الثاني، فبالحيثية الثانية سبب وبالحيثية الأولى مسبب ففيه أن المفاد من التعريف اللفظي إحضار ذات اللفظ الأول بتوسط اللفظ الثاني، لا إحضاره مقيداً بكونه مدلول اللفظ الأول بتوسط إحضاره مقيداً بكونه مدلول اللفظ الثاني . قوله : ( إنما المراد إلخ ) إذ معنى قولنا الغضنفر الأسد أن ما وضع له الغضنفر هو ما وضع له الأسد، فالمستفاد منه تعيين ما وضع له لفظ الغضنفر، والعلم بوضعه له وفيه رد على المحقق التفتازاني، حيث ذهب إلى أن التعريف اللفظي من المطالب التصورية وقال في شرح الشرح : الحد اللفظي عند المحققين هو أن يقصد بيان ما تعقله الواضع فوضع الاسم بإزائه سواء كان بلفظ مرادف أو باللوازم أو بالذاتيات وبهذا عرف الحد الاسمي في التلويح، فجعل اللفظي والاسمي مترادفين وقال الشارح في حواشي العضدي : وإنما أتى عليه من عدم التدرب بالصناعة وقلة التدبر في مقاصد القوم، والاغترار بمجرد اطلاقهم الاسمي في مقام اللفظي، وقال المحقق الدواني : وأنت خبير بأنه إذا كان الغرض معرفة حال اللفظ أنه موضوع لذلك المعنى، كان بحثاً لغوياً خارجاً عن المطالب التصورية، وأما إذا كان الغرض منه تصور معنى اللفظ أي إحضاره، فليس كذلك كما إذا قلنا : الغضنفر موجود فلم يفهم السامع من الغضنفر معنى، ففسرناه بالأسد ليحصل له تصور معناه، فذلك من المطالب التصورية انتهى، وفيه أن هذا التفسير لإحضار صورة حاصلة ليحكم عليه بموجود وليس كل ما يفيد إحضار صورة حاصلة تعريفاً لفظياً، وإلا لكان الألفاظ المعلومة ،أوضاعها تعريفات لفظية لكونها مفيدة إحضار صورة حاصلة، بل هو ما يفيد إحضار صورة حاصلة، وليعلم منه بأن اللفظ موضوع بازائها كقولنا : الغضنفر الأسد على أنه يرد على قوله ففسرنا بالأسد ليحصل معناه أنه إن أراد به أن التفسير يفيد حصول المعنى ابتداء فممنوع، وإن أراد به أنه يفيد بتوسط إفادته العلم بأنه موضوع له ،فمسلم، لكن حينئذ يكون التفسير المذكور للعلم بالوضع وحصول المعنى يتبعه فتدبر.
And the second [is] the verbal definition (al-taʿrīf al-lafẓī), which is that the word is not clear in indication to a meaning, so it is interpreted by a word clearer in indication to that meaning, like your saying: al-ghaḍanfar is the lion. And this is not a real definition intended to produce a conception not already obtained; rather, the intention is to determine what the word 'al-ghaḍanfar' was coined for among other meanings, so that one attends to that. His saying: (and this is not a real definition etc.) because a real definition is that whose conception is a cause of another conception, and since in verbal definition there is no diversity except in terms of wording, there are not two conceptions diverse in essence or even in consideration, let alone one being a cause of the other. And what is said: that the concept insofar as it is the signification of the first word is other than itself insofar as it is the signification of the second word, so by the second relativity it is a cause and by the first it is an effect — in it [is] that the import of verbal definition is to present the essence of the first word by means of the second word, not to present it restricted by being the signification of the first word by means of presenting it restricted by being the signification of the second word. His saying: (rather the intention etc.) because the meaning of our saying 'al-ghaḍanfar is the lion' is that what al-ghaḍanfar was coined for is what the lion was coined for, so what is derived from it is the determination of what the word 'al-ghaḍanfar' was coined for, and knowledge that it was coined for it. In it is a refutation of the investigator al-Taftazani, who held that verbal definition is among the conceptual demands (al-maṭālib al-taṣawwuriyya) and said in Sharḥ al-Sharḥ: The verbal definition according to the investigators is that one intends to explain what the coiner conceived and therefore placed the name for it, whether with a synonymous word, or with concomitants, or with essences; and by this the nominal definition (al-ḥadd al-ismī) was defined in al-Talwīḥ, thus he made the verbal and the nominal synonymous. And the commentator said in the glosses of al-ʿAḍudī: He was only brought to this by lack of training in the craft and lack of reflection on the aims of the people, and being deceived by their mere using of 'nominal' in the place of 'verbal'. And the investigator al-Dawānī said: And you are experienced that if the purpose is to know the state of the word — that it is coined for that meaning — then it is a linguistic inquiry outside the conceptual demands; but if the purpose is to conceive the meaning of the word, i.e., to present it, then it is not so, as when we say: al-ghaḍanfar is existent, and the listener did not understand a meaning from al-ghaḍanfar, so we interpreted it by 'lion' to obtain for him its conception — that is from the conceptual demands. End. And in it [i.e., in this view] is that this interpretation is to present an already obtained picture in order to judge it as existent, and not everything that yields the presentation of an already obtained picture is a verbal definition; otherwise known words whose coinages are known would be verbal definitions because they yield the presentation of an already obtained picture. Rather, it is what yields the presentation of an already obtained picture and also conveys that the word is coined for it, like our saying: al-ghaḍanfar is the lion. And it is objected to his saying: 'so we interpreted it by 'lion' to obtain its meaning' that if he means that the interpretation yields the initial attainment of the meaning, it is denied; if he means that it yields by means of conveying knowledge that it is coined for it, it is conceded; but then that interpretation is for the knowledge of the coinage, and the attainment of the meaning follows. So consider carefully.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage discusses verbal definition (al-taʿrīf al-lafẓī), which is used when a word is not clear in its indication; it is then explained by a more clearly indicative word, such as 'al-ghaḍanfar is the lion'. The passage argues that this is not a real definition intended to produce a new conception; rather, it simply assigns the word's referent. The commentary elaborates that a real definition involves a conception that causes another conception, but in verbal definition, there is no diversity of conceptions, only a diversity in wording. A potential counterargument—that the concept as signified by the first word is different from the concept as signified by the second—is rejected because verbal definition only presents the essence of the first word, not the concept under a description. The passage then addresses a debate: al-Taftazani considered verbal definition as a conceptual demand, but the commentator refutes this, citing al-Dawani's distinction: if the aim is to know the word's coinage, it is linguistic; if to conceive the meaning, it is conceptual. However, the commentator further criticizes al-Dawani, arguing that not every presentation of an already known picture is a verbal definition; it must also inform that the word is coined for that picture. The example 'al-ghaḍanfar is the lion' achieves both. The passage ends with a careful nuance: the interpretation yields meaning only indirectly through knowledge of coinage.

Key Terms
تعريف لفظي
تعريف حقيقي
مطالب تصورية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Verbal definition produces new conceptual knowledge.
Correction: Verbal definition only clarifies the referent; it does not introduce a new concept.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main purpose of a verbal definition?
A) To provide a complete conceptual analysis of a term
B) To determine what a word was coined for among other meanings
C) To teach a new concept through synonyms
D) To prove the existence of the defined object

Key Takeaway
Verbal definition resolves which meaning a word refers to, not what that meaning is.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
هل سبق لك أن شعرت بأن مجرد معرفتك لمصطلح شرعي (مثل التوحيد أو الإيمان) من خلال تعريفه اللفظي (مثل 'الإيمان بالله وحده') يعطيك فهماً كاملاً، بينما في الحقيقة تفتقر إلى التصور الحقيقي العميق؟ كيف يكشف لك هذا الدرس عن خداع الذات؟ وما الخطوة العملية التي ستتخذها اليوم لانتقال من الألفة اللفظية إلى التصور الحقيقي؟
?
عند مناقشة المسائل العقدية مع الآخرين، هل تعتمد غالباً على التعريفات اللفظية لتظهر بمظهر العالم، بينما فهمك الفعلي للمفاهيم سطحي؟ كيف يمكنك التحقق من أن فهمك حقيقي لا لفظي؟ اذكر شيئاً واحداً ستغيره في طريقة تعلمك.
?
يميز المصنف بين إحضار ذات اللفظ الأول (المعنى نفسه) وإحضاره تحت وصف كونه مدلول اللفظ الأول. في طلبك للعلم، هل تسعى إلى ذات الحقائق التي جاء بها القرآن والسنة، أم تكتفي بتحديد ما تشير إليه الألفاظ؟ التزم بعمل عملي واحد لتعميق تصورك لمفهوم عقدي تعلمته مؤخراً.
